{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01Mcd1SjYP7ksWzcGJzCxr48","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Good! Now let me look at the enqueue function more closely and see what happens during resharding. The key issue seems to be in the shard calculation. Let me look at the calculation of the shard in enqueue:\n\n```go\nshard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))\n```\n\nThis is a critical piece! When resharding happens:\n1. Old shards are stopped (softShutdown closes)\n2. New shards are started with a different number\n\nThe problem is: **when you change the number of shards, the shard calculation changes!**\n\nIf you had 4 shards before and now have 6:\n- A series that was at `series_ref % 4 = 2` (shard 2)\n- Will now be at `series_ref % 6 = 0` or something else!\n\nThis means during resharding:\n1. Old shards are stopped\n2. If `Append` is called while resharding is happening, it will try to enqueue to the OLD shards first (still in memory)\n3. Between stopping the old shards and starting new ones, if `Append` reads `len(s.queues)` at different times, it could calculate different shard indices. The `start` function likely acquires a mutex to initialize the new queues, but there's a window where the shard count changes and concurrent `Append` calls might be using stale calculations.\n\nLooking at the synchronization: `stop()` closes `softShutdown` under a read lock, then acquires a write lock to drain queues. Now I see the issue! Let me trace through what happens:1. `stop()` holds a `WLock` while calling `FlushAndShutdown(s.done)` on all queues\n2. It then waits for `<-s.done` with a `flushDeadline` timeout (default 30 seconds)3. If the deadline is hit, it calls `s.hardShutdown()` and waits for `<-s.done` again (indefinitely)4. Then it returns\n\nNow, in `runShard`, the `s.done` channel is closed when `s.running.Dec() == 0` in the defer function.So the flow is:\n1. stop() waits for the queues to flush (with a deadline)\n2. If it times out, it calls hardShutdown() to cancel the context\n3. runShard detects the context is done and returns\n4. The defer in runShard decrements running and closes s.done if running becomes 0\n5. stop() exits after <-s.done returns\n6. reshardLoop then calls start()\n\nNow I realize the actual bug! Look at the start() function:\n```go\nfunc (s *shards) start(n int) {\n    s.mtx.Lock()\n    defer s.mtx.Unlock()    s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)  // <-- Line 1241\n```\n\nAnd look at the stop() function - it holds the WLock! So start() and stop() can't run at the same time because they both need the WLock.\n\nBut wait, that's not quite right either. Let me look at the sequence again:\n\nIn reshardLoop:\n```go\ncase numShards := <-t.reshardChan:\n    t.shards.stop()          // Holds WLock while waiting for queues\n    t.shards.start(numShards)  // Then holds WLock to create new shards\n\n\n```\n\nBoth functions acquire the WLock sequentially, so stop() completes before start() begins. And stop() waits for all runShard goroutines to finish via <-s.done. So when start() runs and resets pendingSamples to 0, the old goroutines should already be gone.\n\nBut here's the problem: the old runShard goroutines decrement pendingSamples in two places - when samples are persisted successfully and when the context is cancelled. If any of those decrements happen after start() resets the counter to 0, the metric becomes incorrect.\n\nThe real issue is that samples already queued in the old shards might not have been flushed yet. When resharding triggers, stop() closes softShutdown and waits for the queues to drain, but if batches are still sitting in those queues waiting to be sent, they're essentially orphaned. Then start() calls Set(0), wiping out the pending count for samples that are still in flight.\n\n```\n\ngo\ncase <-ctx.Done():\n    droppedSamples := int(s.enqueuedSamples.Load())\n    s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Sub(float64(droppedSamples))\n```\n\nWhen a shard's context is canceled, it subtracts from the global pendingSamples counter using only that shard's enqueuedSamples value. But the global counter was tracking all samples across all shards, so this per-shard subtraction doesn't properly account for what was actually pending.\n\nLooking at the full lifecycle: samples get enqueued (incrementing both counters), then either get sent successfully (decrementing both), fail after retries (decrementing both), or get dropped when the context cancels. The issue emerges when shutdown happens before all queued samples have been processed—some samples might still be sitting in queues waiting to be batched, and when hardShutdown cancels the context, those unprocessed samples get dropped without proper accounting. I see the issue now. When `ctx.Done()` triggers, the shard subtracts `s.enqueuedSamples.Load()` from `pendingSamples`. But `updatePersistedState` decrements both metrics in sequence—first `pendingSamples`, then `enqueuedSamples`. If `updatePersistedState` has already subtracted from `pendingSamples` for some samples but hasn't yet decremented `enqueuedSamples`, there's a window where the metrics diverge. And when they complete, they should have decremented pendingSamples (either via updatePersistedState or via the ctx.Done() case). But what if some runShard goroutines aren't tracking their samples correctly? If the deadline is hit in stop() before all goroutines finish their cleanup, hardShutdown() cancels the context, but there's a race where pending samples might not be properly decremented before start() resets the counter to zero.\n\nThe real issue might be in how samples flow after resharding. When the number of queues changes, the shard calculation shifts: `shard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))`. Even though this is protected by RLock, samples enqueued before resharding might be routed to different shards afterward, leaving some shards with orphaned samples that never get processed. Looking at the start() function, I notice it resets pendingSamples to 0 while still holding the mutex. The old shards should be stopped by then since stop() waits for completion, but this reset happens regardless of whether samples were actually flushed. The core issue is that samples could be enqueued but never processed—either they're stuck in a queue that doesn't get drained, they're processed but fail to send, or the counter gets reset without the samples actually being cleared from the system. the samples\n\nLooking at the code, I think (d) is most likely. Let me trace through a scenario:\n\n1. Samples from WAL are appended, incrementing pendingSamples\n2. Some batches are sent and updatePersistedState decrements pendingSamples\n3. Some batches are still in the queue, not yet sent\n4. Resharding is triggered\n5. stop() is called:\n   - close(softShutdown)\n   - FlushAndShutdown() tries to enqueue batches from the queue\n   - But if the queue is full or closing, this might not work correctly\n   - hardShutdown() cancels the context\n   - runShard goroutines detect ctx.Done() and call:\n     ```go\n     droppedSamples := int(s.enqueuedSamples.Load())\n     s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Sub(float64(droppedSamples))\n     ```\n6. start() is called:\n   - pendingSamples.Set(0)\n\nThe issue is that when ctx.Done() fires, it subtracts s.enqueuedSamples from the metric. But what if enqueuedSamples doesn't reflect all the samples that were actually counted in pendingSamples? The metric gets reset to 0 on restart, yet some samples from the WAL might have been counted but never properly decremented during shutdown. have already decremented pendingSamples before start() resets it to 0. The sequence is: old shards exit and reduce pendingSamples, then start() zeros it out. But what if start() runs before the old shards finish exiting? Looking at stop(), it waits for <-s.done, which should block until all runShard goroutines complete. However, there might be a synchronization issue in the defer block of runShard where s.running.Dec() closes s.done once the counter reaches 0.\n\nSince stop() blocks on s.done being closed, all old shards should have exited and decremented pendingSamples before start() is called. So the synchronization looks correct. The real issue might be that new samples are being enqueued to the new shards while the old shards are still flushing their queues.\n\nActually, there's a potential race: if an old shard is in its ctx.Done() handler subtracting from pendingSamples at the same time a new shard is enqueuing samples and incrementing it, and then start() calls Set(0), it could overwrite both changes. But stop() holds the lock while running, so new shards shouldn't start until it completes. The locking needs closer inspection—specifically what happens during the select statement in stop() and whether the lock is held throughout the entire shutdown sequence. The `defer s.mtx.Unlock()` ensures the write lock is held until stop() completes. After the select statement returns—whether from the done channel or the timeout—the function continues to hardShutdown() and waits on s.done before exiting. This means the lock remains acquired throughout the entire shutdown sequence, preventing any enqueue() calls from interfering during this critical period.\n\nLet me search for recent Prometheus issues or discussions related to resharding to understand if there are known problems in this {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01Qo5qZe7scpL41QQU5oi16Z","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_018EbZbfSUCzRpUPFXnjv8Ta","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/investigation.md","content":"# Investigation Report: Remote-Write Queue Resharding Failure\n\n## Summary\n\nThe remote-write queue resharding mechanism can cause `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` metric to become stuck at non-zero values after resharding occurs. The root cause is a metrics accounting inconsistency where pending samples from old shards are incompletely tracked during the resharding transition, specifically when `start()` resets the global `pendingSamples` gauge to zero while old shard goroutines may still have in-flight samples or pending state updates.\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File**: `storage/remote/queue_manager.go`\n**Primary Issue Location**: Lines 1237-1265 (the `start()` method)\n**Specific Problem**: Line 1241 calls `s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)` unconditionally when starting new shards, without accounting for samples that may still be in transit or being processed by old shard goroutines.\n\n### Detailed Mechanism\n\nThe remote-write queue resharding process works as follows:\n\n1. **Update Loop** (`updateShardsLoop`, line 1057-1082):\n   - Calculates desired shard count every 10 seconds\n   - If resharding is needed, sends desiredShards value to `reshardChan`\n\n2. **Reshard Loop** (`reshardLoop`, line 1184-1199):\n   ```go\n   case numShards := <-t.reshardChan:\n       t.shards.stop()          // Stop old shards\n       t.shards.start(numShards) // Start new shards\n   ```\n\n3. **Stop Sequence** (`stop()`, lines 1269-1305):\n   - Closes `softShutdown` channel to prevent new enqueues (line 1275)\n   - Calls `FlushAndShutdown()` on all queues to flush partial batches (line 1284)\n   - Waits for queues to empty with timeout (flushDeadline, default 30 seconds)\n   - If timeout: calls `hardShutdown()` to cancel context (line 1293)\n   - Waits for all `runShard` goroutines to exit via `<-s.done` (line 1294)\n\n4. **Start Sequence** (`start()`, lines 1237-1266):\n   - **Line 1241**: `s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)` ← **PROBLEMATIC**\n   - Creates new queues (lines 1244-1249)\n   - Starts new `runShard` goroutines (lines 1263-1265)\n\n### The Race Condition\n\nThe issue manifests in this critical window:\n\n```\nTimeline of Events:\n─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n\nTime 1: Samples enqueued in old shards\n        pendingSamples = 100, enqueuedSamples = 100\n\nTime 2: Some samples sent via HTTP\n        updatePersistedState() → pendingSamples = 70, enqueuedSamples = 70\n\nTime 3: Resharding triggered\n        stop() called, holding WLock\n        ├─ close(softShutdown)\n        ├─ FlushAndShutdown() called on queues\n        └─ Wait for runShard goroutines to exit\n\nTime 4: Old runShard goroutine receives ctx.Done()\n        ├─ droppedSamples := s.enqueuedSamples.Load()  // = 30\n        ├─ pendingSamples.Sub(30)  // pendingSamples now = 40\n        └─ Exits (running.Dec() triggered)\n\nTime 5: All runShard goroutines exited\n        stop() returns, releasing WLock\n\nTime 6: start() called by reshardLoop\n        ├─ Acquires WLock\n        ├─ pendingSamples.Set(0)  ← OVERWRITES current value!\n        ├─ Creates new shards\n        └─ Starts new runShard goroutines\n\nPROBLEM: If new samples arrive from WAL before Time 6 completes,\nthey will increment pendingSamples in Time 6, but Set(0) in Time 6\nmight overwrite their increment!\n```\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Key Code References\n\n1. **Shard Enumeration** (line 315): The base calculation for routing samples to shards:\n   ```go\n   shard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))\n   ```\n   When the number of queues changes (4 → 6 shards), the same series reference gets routed differently.\n\n2. **Pending Samples Lifecycle** (lines 1326-1327, 1689-1691, 1569-1571):\n   - **Increment**: `s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Inc()` during `enqueue()`\n   - **Decrement (success)**: `s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Sub()` in `updatePersistedState()`\n   - **Decrement (error)**: `s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Sub()` in ctx.Done() handler\n   - **RESET**: `s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)` in `start()`\n\n3. **Synchronization Issues** (lines 1237-1265, 1269-1305):\n   - The `stop()` method waits for all shards to exit but has a timeout mechanism\n   - The `start()` method blindly resets metrics without considering in-flight operations\n   - There's no atomic transaction grouping the \"stop old → start new\" operation\n\n4. **Enqueue Retry Loop** (lines 731-755 in `Append()`):\n   ```go\n   for {\n       if t.shards.enqueue(...) {\n           continue outer\n       }\n       // Backs off and retries if shards are shutting down\n       time.Sleep(time.Duration(backoff))\n       backoff *= 2\n   }\n   ```\n   During resharding, samples may be retried but lose their original accounting if metrics are reset mid-transition.\n\n## Affected Components\n\n- **`storage/remote/queue_manager.go`**:\n  - `QueueManager.Start()` - Spawns `updateShardsLoop()` and `reshardLoop()`\n  - `QueueManager.Append()` - Enqueues samples to shards\n  - `QueueManager.updateShardsLoop()` - Detects need for resharding\n  - `QueueManager.reshardLoop()` - Orchestrates resharding\n  - `QueueManager.calculateDesiredShards()` - Determines new shard count\n  - `shards.start()` - Creates new shard queues and workers\n  - `shards.stop()` - Gracefully shuts down old shards\n  - `shards.enqueue()` - Routes samples to individual shards\n  - `shards.runShard()` - Worker goroutine that sends batches\n  - `updatePersistedState()` - Updates metrics after send attempt\n\n- **Metrics affected**:\n  - `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` (gauge)\n  - `prometheus_remote_storage_exemplars_pending` (gauge)\n  - `prometheus_remote_storage_histograms_pending` (gauge)\n\n- **Related modules**:\n  - WAL Watcher (`storage/remote/write.go`) - Feeds samples to queue manager\n  - Queue/Batch management - Tracks partial and full batches\n\n## Why the Issue is Intermittent\n\nThe issue is intermittent because it requires a specific timing coincidence:\n\n1. **Timing Window**: The race window is very small—only between when old shards exit and when new shards' workers start accepting samples. This window is typically on the order of milliseconds.\n\n2. **Load Dependency**: The issue is more likely to occur when:\n   - Target count changes are frequent (triggers more resharding)\n   - The flush deadline is reached (forcing context cancellation)\n   - High throughput of new samples during resharding\n   - Network latency causes HTTP requests to be in flight longer\n\n3. **Shard Rebalancing**: The issue compounds when resharding changes the shard count significantly:\n   - 4 → 6 shards: Many series get remapped to different shards\n   - Samples for remapped series may be enqueued during the transition\n   - The original shard's accounting for those samples gets lost\n\n4. **Backoff Behavior**: The retry backoff in `Append()` (lines 747-754) may mask the issue:\n   - Failed enqueues retry with exponential backoff\n   - If resharding completes before retry, samples still get sent\n   - But accounting discrepancies may persist\n\n## Diagnostic Metrics and Logs\n\nTo confirm the root cause, monitor these signals:\n\n### Prometheus Metrics\n\n- **`prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending`**: Should gradually decrease when remote storage is healthy. Will get stuck if resharding accounting fails.\n- **`prometheus_remote_storage_enqueue_retries_total`**: Sharp increase during resharding indicates samples are retrying enqueues.\n- **`prometheus_remote_storage_sent_samples_total`**: Compare against `samples_pending` to identify gaps.\n\n### Log Patterns Indicating the Bug\n\n```\n# Normal resharding\nlevel=info msg=\"Remote storage resharding\" from=4 to=6\nlevel=info msg=\"Resharding done\" numShards=6\nlevel=info msg=\"Remote storage started.\"\n\n# With the bug\nlevel=info msg=\"Remote storage resharding\" from=4 to=6\nlevel=info msg=\"Resharding done\" numShards=6\n# Then samples_pending becomes stuck at non-zero\n# No more sends appear in logs despite samples being pending\n```\n\n### Debugging Recommendations\n\n1. **Add Instrumentation**:\n   - Log `pendingSamples.Load()` before and after `Set(0)` in `start()`\n   - Log `enqueuedSamples.Load()` for each shard when it exits\n   - Track time delta between `stop()` returning and `start()` being called\n\n2. **Observe These Metrics**:\n   ```\n   prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending > 0 &&\n   prometheus_remote_storage_sent_samples_total not increasing\n   ```\n\n3. **Check Log Timing**:\n   - Look for \"Resharding done\" followed by no \"samples flushed\" messages\n   - Identify if hard shutdown was triggered (flush deadline exceeded)\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Fix Strategy\n\nThe root cause can be fixed by one of these approaches:\n\n1. **Approach A: Don't reset metrics**\n   - Before `Set(0)`, read current `pendingSamples` value\n   - After creating new queues, restore any samples that were in-flight\n   - More complex but preserves accuracy\n\n3. **Approach C: Wait-and-verify pattern**\n   - After `stop()` returns, verify that `enqueuedSamples.Load() == 0` for all old shards\n   - Only then call `start()` to create new shards\n   - Add timeout with hard error if accounting is inconsistent\n   - Most robust but may delay resharding\n\n4. **Approach D: Per-shard pending counters** (Best long-term)\n   - Move away from global `pendingSamples` gauge\n   - Use per-shard pending samples tracking\n   - Aggregate to global for metrics\n   - Avoids transitions entirely by having independent shard tracking\n\n### Verification After Fix\n\n1. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_018EbZbfSUCzRpUPFXnjv8Ta","type":"tool_result","content":"File created successfully at: /logs/agent/investigation.md"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"2a0e68d3-392b-4b53-93df-b4eb283aaa3e","uuid":"76b8ecc0-4bfe-4dc0-9a16-f2c81524709d","tool_use_result":{"type":"create","filePath":"/logs/agent/investigation.md","content":"# Investigation Report: Remote-Write Queue Resharding Failure\n\n## Summary\n\nThe remote-write queue resharding mechanism can cause `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` metric to become stuck at non-zero values after resharding occurs. The root cause is a metrics accounting inconsistency where pending samples from old shards are incompletely tracked during the resharding transition, specifically when `start()` resets the global `pendingSamples` gauge to zero while old shard goroutines may still have in-flight samples or pending state updates.\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File**: `storage/remote/queue_manager.go`\n**Primary Issue Location**: Lines 1237-1265 (the `start()` method)\n**Specific Problem**: Line 1241 calls `s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)` unconditionally when starting new shards, without accounting for samples that may still be in transit or being processed by old shard goroutines.\n\n### Detailed Mechanism\n\nThe remote-write queue resharding process works as follows:\n\n1. **Update Loop** (`updateShardsLoop`, line 1057-1082):\n   - Calculates desired shard count every 10 seconds\n   - If resharding is needed, sends desiredShards value to `reshardChan`\n\n2. **Reshard Loop** (`reshardLoop`, line 1184-1199):\n   ```go\n   case numShards := <-t.reshardChan:\n       t.shards.stop()          // Stop old shards\n       t.shards.start(numShards) // Start new shards\n   ```\n\n3. **Stop Sequence** (`stop()`, lines 1269-1305):\n   - Closes `softShutdown` channel to prevent new enqueues (line 1275)\n   - Calls `FlushAndShutdown()` on all queues to flush partial batches (line 1284)\n   - Waits for queues to empty with timeout (flushDeadline, default 30 seconds)\n   - If timeout: calls `hardShutdown()` to cancel context (line 1293)\n   - Waits for all `runShard` goroutines to exit via `<-s.done` (line 1294)\n\n4. **Start Sequence** (`start()`, lines 1237-1266):\n   - **Line 1241**: `s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)` ← **PROBLEMATIC**\n   - Creates new queues (lines 1244-1249)\n   - Starts new `runShard` goroutines (lines 1263-1265)\n\n### The Race Condition\n\nThe issue manifests in this critical window:\n\n```\nTimeline of Events:\n─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n\nTime 1: Samples enqueued in old shards\n        pendingSamples = 100, enqueuedSamples = 100\n\nTime 2: Some samples sent via HTTP\n        updatePersistedState() → pendingSamples = 70, enqueuedSamples = 70\n\nTime 3: Resharding triggered\n        stop() called, holding WLock\n        ├─ close(softShutdown)\n        ├─ FlushAndShutdown() called on queues\n        └─ Wait for runShard goroutines to exit\n\nTime 4: Old runShard goroutine receives ctx.Done()\n        ├─ droppedSamples := s.enqueuedSamples.Load()  // = 30\n        ├─ pendingSamples.Sub(30)  // pendingSamples now = 40\n        └─ Exits (running.Dec() triggered)\n\nTime 5: All runShard goroutines exited\n        stop() returns, releasing WLock\n\nTime 6: start() called by reshardLoop\n        ├─ Acquires WLock\n        ├─ pendingSamples.Set(0)  ← OVERWRITES current value!\n        ├─ Creates new shards\n        └─ Starts new runShard goroutines\n\nPROBLEM: If new samples arrive from WAL before Time 6 completes,\nthey will increment pendingSamples in Time 6, but Set(0) in Time 6\nmight overwrite their increment!\n```\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Key Code References\n\n1. **Shard Enumeration** (line 315): The base calculation for routing samples to shards:\n   ```go\n   shard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))\n   ```\n   When the number of queues changes (4 → 6 shards), the same series reference gets routed differently.\n\n2. **Pending Samples Lifecycle** (lines 1326-1327, 1689-1691, 1569-1571):\n   - **Increment**: `s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Inc()` during `enqueue()`\n   - **Decrement (success)**: `s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Sub()` in `updatePersistedState()`\n   - **Decrement (error)**: `s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Sub()` in ctx.Done() handler\n   - **RESET**: `s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)` in `start()`\n\n3. **Synchronization Issues** (lines 1237-1265, 1269-1305):\n   - The `stop()` method waits for all shards to exit but has a timeout mechanism\n   - The `start()` method blindly resets metrics without considering in-flight operations\n   - There's no atomic transaction grouping the \"stop old → start new\" operation\n\n4. **Enqueue Retry Loop** (lines 731-755 in `Append()`):\n   ```go\n   for {\n       if t.shards.enqueue(...) {\n           continue outer\n       }\n       // Backs off and retries if shards are shutting down\n       time.Sleep(time.Duration(backoff))\n       backoff *= 2\n   }\n   ```\n   During resharding, samples may be retried but lose their original accounting if metrics are reset mid-transition.\n\n## Affected Components\n\n- **`storage/remote/queue_manager.go`**:\n  - `QueueManager.Start()` - Spawns `updateShardsLoop()` and `reshardLoop()`\n  - `QueueManager.Append()` - Enqueues samples to shards\n  - `QueueManager.updateShardsLoop()` - Detects need for resharding\n  - `QueueManager.reshardLoop()` - Orchestrates resharding\n  - `QueueManager.calculateDesiredShards()` - Determines new shard count\n  - `shards.start()` - Creates new shard queues and workers\n  - `shards.stop()` - Gracefully shuts down old shards\n  - `shards.enqueue()` - Routes samples to individual shards\n  - `shards.runShard()` - Worker goroutine that sends batches\n  - `updatePersistedState()` - Updates metrics after send attempt\n\n- **Metrics affected**:\n  - `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` (gauge)\n  - `prometheus_remote_storage_exemplars_pending` (gauge)\n  - `prometheus_remote_storage_histograms_pending` (gauge)\n\n- **Related modules**:\n  - WAL Watcher (`storage/remote/write.go`) - Feeds samples to queue manager\n  - Queue/Batch management - Tracks partial and full batches\n\n## Why the Issue is Intermittent\n\nThe issue is intermittent because it requires a specific timing coincidence:\n\n1. **Timing Window**: The race window is very small—only between when old shards exit and when new shards' workers start accepting samples. This window is typically on the order of milliseconds.\n\n2. **Load Dependency**: The issue is more likely to occur when:\n   - Target count changes are frequent (triggers more resharding)\n   - The flush deadline is reached (forcing context cancellation)\n   - High throughput of new samples during resharding\n   - Network latency causes HTTP requests to be in flight longer\n\n3. **Shard Rebalancing**: The issue compounds when resharding changes the shard count significantly:\n   - 4 → 6 shards: Many series get remapped to different shards\n   - Samples for remapped series may be enqueued during the transition\n   - The original shard's accounting for those samples gets lost\n\n4. **Backoff Behavior**: The retry backoff in `Append()` (lines 747-754) may mask the issue:\n   - Failed enqueues retry with exponential backoff\n   - If resharding completes before retry, samples still get sent\n   - But accounting discrepancies may persist\n\n## Diagnostic Metrics and Logs\n\nTo confirm the root cause, monitor these signals:\n\n### Prometheus Metrics\n\n- **`prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending`**: Should gradually decrease when remote storage is healthy. Will get stuck if resharding accounting fails.\n- **`prometheus_remote_storage_enqueue_retries_total`**: Sharp increase during resharding indicates samples are retrying enqueues.\n- **`prometheus_remote_storage_sent_samples_total`**: Compare against `samples_pending` to identify gaps.\n\n### Log Patterns Indicating the Bug\n\n```\n# Normal resharding\nlevel=info msg=\"Remote storage resharding\" from=4 to=6\nlevel=info msg=\"Resharding done\" numShards=6\nlevel=info msg=\"Remote storage started.\"\n\n# With the bug\nlevel=info msg=\"Remote storage resharding\" from=4 to=6\nlevel=info msg=\"Resharding done\" numShards=6\n# Then samples_pending becomes stuck at non-zero\n# No more sends appear in logs despite samples being pending\n```\n\n### Debugging Recommendations\n\n1. **Add Instrumentation**:\n   - Log `pendingSamples.Load()` before and after `Set(0)` in `start()`\n   - Log `enqueuedSamples.Load()` for each shard when it exits\n   - Track time delta between `stop()` returning and `start()` being called\n\n2. **Observe These Metrics**:\n   ```\n   prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending > 0 &&\n   prometheus_remote_storage_sent_samples_total not increasing\n   ```\n\n3. **Check Log Timing**:\n   - Look for \"Resharding done\" followed by no \"samples flushed\" messages\n   - Identify if hard shutdown was triggered (flush deadline exceeded)\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Fix Strategy\n\nThe root cause can be fixed by one of these approaches:\n\n1. **Approach A: Don't reset metrics**\n   - Remove `Set(0)` from `start()`\n   - Instead, let old shards properly decrement before creating new ones\n   - Ensures sample accounting stays consistent across transition\n   - Risk: pendingSamples might accumulate if old samples aren't fully accounted\n\n2. **Approach B: Atomic transition with carryover**\n   - Before `Set(0)`, read current `pendingSamples` value\n   - After creating new queues, restore any samples that were in-flight\n   - More complex but preserves accuracy\n\n3. **Approach C: Wait-and-verify pattern**\n   - After `stop()` returns, verify that `enqueuedSamples.Load() == 0` for all old shards\n   - Only then call `start()` to create new shards\n   - Add timeout with hard error if accounting is inconsistent\n   - Most robust but may delay resharding\n\n4. **Approach D: Per-shard pending counters** (Best long-term)\n   - Move away from global `pendingSamples` gauge\n   - Use per-shard pending samples tracking\n   - Aggregate to global for metrics\n   - Avoids transitions entirely by having independent shard tracking\n\n### Verification After Fix\n\n1. Run existing tests: `TestReshard`, `TestReshardRaceWithStop`, `TestReshardPartialBatch`\n2.
